     1	# Phase 2 — Exhaustive Audit of nirs4all Documentation & Examples
     2	
     3	**Date:** 2026-06-04 · **Library version of record:** 0.9.1 · **License of record:** AGPL-3.0
     4	**Method:** ground-truth-first, 22-agent grounded fan-out, adversarial completeness critic, manual verification pass, Codex-gated.
     5	**Status:** complete. Raw data in `data/` (`audit_segments.json`, `audit_synthesis.json`, `audit_completeness_critic.json`). Ground-truth card in `GROUND_TRUTH.md`.
     6	
     7	---
     8	
     9	## 0. Verdict
    10	
    11	The corpus is **broad, conceptually strong, and NOT publication-ready.** Mean segment health is **2.80 / 5** across 20 audited segments. The content (concepts, reference tables, scientific prose) is largely *accurate and complete*; what drags it down is **mechanical rot and structural sprawl**, not wrong ideas. Three systemic failures compound to mislead a newcomer within the first ten minutes:
    12	
    13	1. **Metadata drift on first-contact surfaces** — wrong license (CeCILL-2.1 instead of AGPL-3.0) and wrong version (0.2.1 / 0.7.1 / 0.8.6 / 0.9.0 / "5.0" instead of 0.9.1) on the landing page, the citation block, the AI-onboarding page, `conf.py`, and the root `CLAUDE.md`. A wrong license on the landing page is a compliance issue, not a typo.
    14	2. **The inline-pipeline style mandate is violated 648 times across 140 files** (authoritative grep, §3). *No segment is fully clean.* The docs teach, at scale, the exact anti-pattern the project wants forbidden.
    15	3. **Copy-paste-fatal wrong-API references** scattered through the on-ramp and how-to layers (`result.predict()`, `nirs4all.load_dataset()`, `bundle=`, `y_column=`, `PredictionAnalyzer.plot_predictions()`, `GaussianNoise`, `SklearnWrapper`, `examples.synthetic` import, `Predictions.load()` in the shipped notebook) — every one verified against source as non-existent.
    16	
    17	Underlying all three is one root cause: **nothing that executes documentation exists in the safety net.** Doc `.md` code blocks are never run; the `examples/*.py` suite (which *does* run) is on a **weekly** schedule, not per-PR; and the Sphinx build actively **suppresses** broken cross-references (`nitpick_ignore_regex` blankets entire `nirs4all.*` namespaces). So every defect above survived precisely because nothing could catch it.
    18	
    19	The good news, and the reason a rewrite is tractable: the failures are **overwhelmingly mechanical and high-reach/low-effort**. A metadata one-commit fix, one mechanical inline-pipeline sweep, a ~15-item wrong-API triage, and a CI gate to stop regression clear the majority. The structural work (collapsing the competing front doors) is design, not archaeology. This audit is the input to the Phase 3 restructuring proposal.
    20	
    21	---
    22	
    23	## 1. Methodology
    24	
    25	Why this much machinery: the user asked for an audit that is *detailed, structured, exhaustive, and justified*, reviewed by Codex at each step. Documentation audits fail in two classic ways — (a) the auditor hallucinates the API and "corrects" things that are actually fine, and (b) coverage is uneven so whole areas are silently skipped. We defended against both:
    26	
    27	- **Ground-truth-first.** Before any agent ran, the real public surface was extracted *directly from source* (`nirs4all/__init__.py`, `nirs4all/api/*.py`, `api/result.py`) into `GROUND_TRUTH.md` — exact `__all__`, signatures, result-object members, the canonical style form. Every agent was required to Read it and to cite the source/ground-truth fact proving each defect (the `evidence` field). No claim rests on memory.
    28	- **Deterministic fan-out.** The doc+example surface was partitioned into **20 segments with explicit, non-overlapping file lists** (12 documentation · 6 examples · 2 root/build) so coverage is provable, not best-effort. One `Explore` (read-only) reader per segment, run in parallel, each grounding against source.
    29	- **Cross-cutting synthesis** (1 agent, barrier): merged duplicate findings, quantified repo-wide patterns, built the prioritized register.
    30	- **Adversarial completeness critic** (1 agent): tasked only with finding what the audit *missed or over-claimed*.
    31	- **Manual verification pass** (this orchestrator, against source): resolved every dispute the critic raised, ran the authoritative style-violation grep, and audited the surfaces the fan-out had missed (the notebook, the hand-written `api/*.md` pages, build hygiene).
    32	- **Codex gate:** the finished audit is handed to Codex (`codex exec`, CLI 0.136.0) for independent adversarial review before Phase 3. Transcript archived under `codex_reviews/`.
    33	
    34	**Run cost (audit workflow):** 22 agents, ~1.73M agent tokens, 1011 tool calls, ~11 min wall-clock. 20/20 segment readers returned. Plus 3 gap-closing agents and the manual verification pass.
    35	
    36	### 1.1 The completeness critic earned its keep — corrections applied
    37	
    38	The critic caught **two false "critical release blockers"** and a **false "clean segment"** claim in the raw synthesis. All three were independently re-verified against source and **corrected** in this document (full transparency in §6):
    39	
    40	| Raw claim | Verdict after verification | Source proof |
    41	|---|---|---|
    42	| "Uninstantiated transform classes → runtime crash" (U01_shap_basics.py) | **FALSE — downgraded.** Bare class types are an *intentional, supported* pipeline form. | `nirs4all/pipeline/steps/parser.py:231` "Class types: returns as-is (controller will instantiate)"; the file is in both CI runners and passes. |
    43	| "Two broken transfer-learning imports → ImportError crash, release blocker" | **PARTLY FALSE — downgraded to medium.** Both imports are inside `try/except ImportError`; they don't crash. But the module paths *are* wrong, so the feature is silently never demonstrated. | `examples/developer/04_transfer_learning/D01_transfer_analysis.py:130-152` (try/except). Real homes: `nirs4all.analysis.selector.TransferPreprocessingSelector`, `nirs4all.visualization.analysis.transfer.PreprocPCAEvaluator`. |
    44	| "Only 2 segments are style-clean; ~250+ violations" | **FALSE.** predictions/deployment is *not* clean; the real count is **648** (§3). | grep of `making_predictions.md:246`, `session_api.md:30,217`; authoritative count in §3. |
    45	
    46	This is the audit doing its job: the multi-agent pass surfaced ~216 candidate defects fast, and the adversarial+manual layer pruned the wrong ones before they could waste a maintainer's time. **Act on the corrected register (§4), not the raw per-segment files.**

    72	## 3. The inline-pipeline style mandate — authoritative measurement
    73	
    74	> **Mandate (user, verbatim intent):** "1 pipeline, des datasets, run()." Pipelines must be written **inline, in one shot**, inside `run()`, with **no external variable**, for readability:
    75	> ```python
    76	> result = nirs4all.run(pipeline=[ ...inline... ], dataset=...)   # ✅
    77	> ```
    78	> ```python
    79	> pipeline = [ ... ]                 # ❌ external variable
    80	> result = nirs4all.run(pipeline, dataset)
    81	> ```
    82	
    83	The raw synthesis estimated "250+ violations, only 2 clean segments." That was wrong (the critic flagged it; one reader's grep was non-uniform). A single uniform grep across `docs/source/**.md` and `examples/**.py` (variable name contains `pipeline`, assigned a list literal at statement level) gives the authoritative figure:
    84	
    85	### **648 violations across 140 files. No segment is clean. 55 compliant inline usages exist.**
    86	
    87	| Area | Violations | Notes |
    88	|---|---:|---|
    89	| `docs/source/user_guide/**` | **224** | epicenter of the how-to layer |
    90	| `examples/user/**` | 132 | the on-ramp the README points to |
    91	| `examples/developer/**` | 99 | branching/generator examples |
    92	| `docs/source/reference/**` | 69 | incl. `pipeline_syntax.md` (47), the canonical syntax page |
    93	| `docs/source/examples/**` (doc pages) | 42 | |
    94	| root `docs/source/*.md` (incl. `ai_onboarding.md` ×16) | 18 | |
    95	| `docs/source/getting_started/**` | 12 | the literal first tutorial |
    96	| `docs/source/concepts/**` | 12 | |
    97	| `docs/source/developer/**` | 10 | |
    98	| `docs/source/onboarding/**` | 7 | |
    99	| `examples/_internal`, `pipeline_samples`, `reference`, `aom_paper` | 23 | mostly non-user-facing tooling |
   100	
   101	**Worst single files:** `user_guide/pipelines/writing_pipelines.md` (51), `reference/pipeline_syntax.md` (47), `user_guide/pipelines/generators.md` (23), `user_guide/models/training.md` (20), `ai_onboarding.md` (16), `examples/user/03_preprocessing/U01_preprocessing_basics.py` (9).
   102	
   103	**Interpretation.** This is a *propagated template defect*, not isolated authoring lapses — the same `pipeline = [...]` skeleton was copied everywhere. That is good news for remediation: a single mechanical sweep clears the overwhelming majority. **But** a documented exception is warranted for two legitimate cases, and the proposal must name them so the pattern does not regenerate:
   104	- **Deliberate reuse / comparison** examples that run the *same* pipeline through several `run()` calls or `PipelineRunner`/`Session` deep-dives (a handful in `06_deployment`, `06_internals`).
   105	- **Synthesis/utility** scripts (`developer/02_generators/D05–D09`, `examples/_internal/*`) that are not pipeline tutorials.
   106	
   107	Even those should be re-examined; most can still be inlined. **A `ruff`/grep CI lint enforcing the inline form on `docs/` and `examples/` is the only durable fix** — without it, 648 becomes 700 by the next release.
   108

   176	
   177	## 5. Gap-closing pass (surfaces the fan-out missed)
   178	
   179	### 5.1 `examples/predictions.ipynb` — the single largest coverage hole
   180	
   181	A 1.8 MB Jupyter notebook ships as an example but is **referenced by no runner and no doc page**, and is executed by **no CI**. It is **stale and unrunnable** against 0.9.1:
   182	- `Predictions.load(path=…)` — **no such method**. `Predictions` has `from_workspace()` / `from_file()` / `from_parquet()` (`nirs4all/data/predictions.py:497,530,548`) and a path-detecting constructor.
   183	- `predictions._storage._df` — **no such attribute**. Internal state is `self._store` / `self._buffer` (`predictions.py:236,240`). The notebook reaches into a private Polars frame that doesn't exist.
   184	
   185	**Health 1/5.** Recommendation: either delete it, or rewrite as a runnable `examples/reference/R04_visualization.py` (conveniently filling the missing-R04 gap, #34) using the public `PredictionAnalyzer` API, and add it to `run_ci_examples.sh`. A shipped, un-CI'd, broken artifact is worse than no artifact.
   186	
   187	### 5.2 Hand-written `api/*.md` pages
   188	
   189	| Page | Health | Key issue |
   190	|---|---|---|
   191	| `api/module_api.md` | 3/5 | predict() doc names `source` (real `model`); fake `ExplainResult.get_feature_importance()`; 1 style violation |
   192	| `api/sklearn_integration.md` | 4/5 | clean; imports verified (`NIRSPipeline`, `NIRSPipelineClassifier` both exported) |
   193	| `api/storage.md` | 2/5 | "Version 5.0"; duplicates `reference/storage.md` (~800 vs ~400 LOC); legacy `runs/` framing |
   194	| `api/workspace.md` | 2/5 | missing "no `runs/`" principle; PipelineLibrary section 100% duplicate of `reference/workspace.md` |
   195	| `reference/api/session.md` | 4/5 | **orphaned** (no toctree); minor unverified property docs |
   196	
   197	**Pattern:** the `api/` tree (4 hand-written pages + 357 autodoc stubs) and the `reference/` tree document the same surface twice. This is a Phase-3 consolidation target: pick one API-reference home.
   198	
   199	### 5.3 Build / RTD hygiene — the root cause of undetected drift
   200	
   201	- **(A) Broken cross-refs are actively suppressed.** `conf.py` `nitpick_ignore_regex` blankets entire namespaces — `nirs4all.data.*`, `nirs4all.pipeline.*`, `nirs4all.api.*` — and `suppress_warnings` includes `myst.xref_missing` and `ref.*`. Any typo'd `:class:` ref in those namespaces is invisible. **And** CI `docs.yml` builds with `-W --keep-going` (strict) while `.readthedocs.yaml` sets `fail_on_warning: false` — CI and the published build disagree on strictness.
   202	- **(B) Asset integrity: clean.** All referenced images exist with alt text. 3 orphaned asset files (#39).
   203	- **(C) Zero doc-snippet execution.** No `doctest` / `nbval` / `myst_nb` / `literalinclude`-exec anywhere. The only executed code is `examples/*.py`, and `examples.yml` runs **weekly (cron Sunday) + manual only — never on push/PR** (the workflow header says so explicitly). This is *why* `result.predict()`, `bundle=`, `plot_predictions()`, `SklearnWrapper`, and the notebook's `Predictions.load()` all survived: nothing executes them, and the one thing that could runs once a week.
   204	
   205	**This is the highest-leverage systemic fix.** A doc-snippet execution gate (or at minimum moving `examples.yml` to per-PR for a fast subset) plus a tightened `nitpick_ignore` converts the entire class of wrong-API defects from "ships silently" to "fails the build."
   206	
   207	---
   208	
   209	## 6. Transparency: false positives caught and corrected
   210	
   211	To keep the register trustworthy, the audit's own mistakes are recorded rather than hidden (full reasoning in §1.1). The raw 22-agent pass produced ~216 candidate defects; verification **downgraded 2 of the 9 raw "criticals"** (bare classes #21, transfer imports #20) and **corrected the headline style count** from "~250, 2 clean segments" to "648, 0 clean segments." The remaining 7 criticals and the confirmed-true HIGH items were each re-verified against source. Net: the register above is the trustworthy artifact; the per-segment JSON in `data/audit_segments.json` is raw input and contains the un-pruned claims.

   242	---
   243	
   244	## 8. What this means for Phase 3 (restructuring)
   245	
   246	The audit converges on a clear mandate for the restructuring proposal:
   247	
   248	1. **One canonical learning path, one source of truth per concept.** The single biggest *structural* defect is the 3–4 competing front doors (`getting_started/` vs `concepts/` vs `onboarding/` vs `ai_onboarding.md`) and the duplicated `api/` ↔ `reference/` trees. Phase 3 must pick a target information architecture (a Diátaxis-style split is the obvious candidate) and assign every existing page a home or a deletion.
   249	2. **The style mandate becomes infrastructure, not aspiration.** "1 pipeline inline + `run()`" must be enforced by a CI lint over `docs/` + `examples/`, with the two documented exceptions, or 648 will regrow.
   250	3. **Documentation must enter the safety net.** Per-PR execution of a fast example subset + a doc-snippet doctest gate + a tightened `nitpick_ignore`. This is what makes the rewrite *stay* correct.
   251	4. **Metadata is sourced from one place.** Version/license/copyright derived from `nirs4all.__version__` and `LICENSE`, with a CI grep gate.
   252	
   253	Phase 3 will deliver the target IA, a page-by-page migration map (keep / merge / rewrite / delete), the enforced style guide, and the CI gates — justified against these findings.
   254

    65	## Canonical usage form to ENFORCE everywhere
    66	
    67	```python
    68	result = nirs4all.run(
    69	    pipeline=[ ...inline steps... ],   # written in one shot, NO external variable
    70	    dataset=...,
    71	)
    72	```
    73	Anti-pattern to flag: `pipeline = [...]` assigned to a variable, then `nirs4all.run(pipeline, ds)`.

docs/_internal/doc_overhaul_2026-06-04/codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt:59:    17	Underlying all three is one root cause: **nothing that executes documentation exists in the safety net.** Doc `.md` code blocks are never run; the `examples/*.py` suite (which *does* run) is on a **weekly** schedule, not per-PR; and the Sphinx build actively **suppresses** broken cross-references (`nitpick_ignore_regex` blankets entire `nirs4all.*` namespaces). So every defect above survived precisely because nothing could catch it.
docs/_internal/doc_overhaul_2026-06-04/codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt:145:   103	**Interpretation.** This is a *propagated template defect*, not isolated authoring lapses — the same `pipeline = [...]` skeleton was copied everywhere. That is good news for remediation: a single mechanical sweep clears the overwhelming majority. **But** a documented exception is warranted for two legitimate cases, and the proposal must name them so the pattern does not regenerate:
docs/_internal/doc_overhaul_2026-06-04/codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt:184:   142	| 19 | **Examples run weekly, not per-PR; doc snippets never run; broken refs suppressed** | `.github/workflows/examples.yml` (cron Sunday), `docs.yml`, `conf.py` `nitpick_ignore_regex` | The safety-net root cause (§5.3). A broken example sits on `main` up to 7 days; `.md` API drift is never caught; `nirs4all.{data,pipeline,api}.*` xrefs are blanket-ignored. |
docs/_internal/doc_overhaul_2026-06-04/codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt:227:   185	**Health 1/5.** Recommendation: either delete it, or rewrite as a runnable `examples/reference/R04_visualization.py` (conveniently filling the missing-R04 gap, #34) using the public `PredictionAnalyzer` API, and add it to `run_ci_examples.sh`. docs/_internal/doc_overhaul_2026-06-04/codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt:245:   203	- **(C) Zero doc-snippet execution.** No `doctest` / `nbval` / `myst_nb` / `literalinclude`-exec anywhere. The only executed code is `examples/*.py`, and `examples.yml` runs **weekly (cron Sunday) + manual only — never on push/PR** (the workflow header says so explicitly). This is *why* `result.predict()`, `bundle=`, `plot_predictions()`, `SklearnWrapper`, and the notebook's `Predictions.load()` all survived: nothing executes them, and the one thing that could runs once a week.
docs/_internal/doc_overhaul_2026-06-04/codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt:247:   205	**This is the highest-leverage systemic fix.** A doc-snippet execution gate (or at minimum moving `examples.yml` to per-PR for a fast subset) plus a tightened `nitpick_ignore` converts the entire class of wrong-API defects from "ships silently" to "fails the build."

docs/_internal/_archives/plot_display_audit_2026-04-01.md:170:Observed reproduction:
docs/_internal/_archives/plot_display_audit_2026-04-01.md:353:I independently verified the claims in this audit against the current codebase. Findings 1, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7 are confirmed exactly as described. All six chart controllers call `plt.show()` directly — several with comments that contradict the code ("Store figure reference - user will call plt.show() at the end" followed immediately by `plt.show()`). `ExecutorBuilder` stores `_save_charts` but never passes it to `PipelineExecutor`. `PredictionAnalyzer` always resolves a default output directory and has no opt-out mechanism. The SHAP module has 8 direct `plt.show()` calls (more than the 4 line ranges cited). The `U04_aggregation.py` manual polling loop is confirmed. The example file count for `plots_visible=args.plots` is slightly higher than stated (33 files, 77 occurrences, vs. the "31 files" cited — minor discrepancy). Finding 2 requires a nuance correction: `PipelineRunner` does alias its `_figure_refs` to the orchestrator's list via direct assignment (`self._figure_refs = self.orchestrator._figure_refs`), so the two references point to the same object. The actual disconnect is between *that* shared list and the `runtime_context.step_runner._figure_refs` that controllers append to during execution — the step runner used at execution time may not be the same object, so figures still fail to propagate upward. The net conclusion is the same, but the diagnosis should be corrected to reflect where the break actually occurs. Overall, this is a well-grounded audit. The recommended fix direction — centralizing plot lifecycle into a single manager, removing direct `plt.show()` from internals, and making flags semantically consistent — is the right approach. I would prioritize Phase 1 items (removing `plt.show()` from controllers, wiring `save_charts`, fixing example flag semantics) as they address the most user-visible pain with minimal architectural risk. The `IndexError` in `spectra.py` noted in the related-issue section should be tracked separately as it indicates an index-bounds assumption that breaks on smaller datasets.

docs/_internal/_archives/synthesis_as_pipeline.md:1067:**Concentration-path length ambiguity**: In the Beer-Lambert law `A = L * C @ E`, multiplying all concentrations by a factor k and dividing path length by k produces identical spectra. Resolution: fix the path length mean to 1.0 and allow concentrations to absorb the scaling. Or use known reference concentrations.
docs/_internal/_archives/synthesis_as_pipeline.md:1069:**Baseline-scatter ambiguity**: A polynomial baseline and the scatter offset `beta` both add low-frequency components. Resolution: fit them jointly (as the reconstruction module does with the combined design matrix), or use physical constraints (baseline should be smooth, scatter offset should be sample-independent in structure).
docs/_internal/_archives/synthesis_as_pipeline.md:1071:**Global slope vs scatter tilt**: The global slope effect and the scatter tilt `gamma*x` are both linear in wavelength. Resolution: absorb one into the other, or constrain one to be sample-independent.

docs/_internal/_archives/design/implementation_roadmap.md:666:This is a mechanical operation. The risk is in missing an import somewhere. Mitigation:
docs/_internal/_archives/design/implementation_roadmap.md:700:**Mitigation:** The RNG contract (Section "Phase 1 RNG Contract") creates the RNG in `fit()` and reuses it in `transform()`. Since the controller clones operators per sample, `fit()` is called once per clone, and `transform()` once per clone. The allocation happens once per sample, not once per feature. This is acceptable — the overhead of `default_rng()` (~1μs) is negligible compared to the actual transform computation (typically 10-1000μs per sample).

     2	PredictionAnalyzer - Orchestrator for prediction analysis and visualization.
     3	
     4	This module provides a unified interface for creating various prediction visualizations.
     5	Delegates to specialized chart classes for rendering.
     6	
     7	Leverages the refactored Predictions API (predictions.top(), PredictionResult, etc.)
     8	for efficient data access and avoids redundant calculations.
     9	
    10	Includes a caching layer (PredictionCache) to avoid recomputing expensive aggregations
    11	when multiple charts use the same parameters.

    30	def _get_default_figures_dir() -> str:
    31	    """Get the default figures output directory.
    32	
    33	    Checks NIRS4ALL_WORKSPACE environment variable first, then falls back
    34	    to ./workspace in the current working directory.
    35	
    36	    Returns:
    37	        Default figures directory path as string.
    38	    """
    39	    env_workspace = os.environ.get("NIRS4ALL_WORKSPACE")
    40	    if env_workspace:
    41	        return str(Path(env_workspace) / "figures")
    42	    return "workspace/figures"
    43	import contextlib
    44	
    45	from nirs4all.core import metrics as evaluator
    46	from nirs4all.core.logging import get_logger
    47	from nirs4all.core.metrics import abbreviate_metric
    48	
    49	logger = get_logger(__name__)
    50	
    51	class PredictionAnalyzer:
    52	    """Orchestrator for prediction analysis and visualization.
    53	
    54	    Provides a unified interface for creating various prediction visualizations.
    55	    Delegates to specialized chart classes for rendering.
    56	
    57	    Includes a caching layer (PredictionCache) to avoid recomputing expensive
    58	    aggregations when multiple charts use the same parameters. The cache is
    59	    keyed by (aggregate, rank_metric, rank_partition, display_partition, group_by,
    60	    filters) and stores the results of predictions.top() calls.
    61	
    62	    Leverages the refactored Predictions API (predictions.top(), PredictionResult, etc.)
    63	    for efficient data access and avoids redundant calculations.
    64	
    65	    Attributes:
    66	        predictions: Predictions object containing prediction data.
    67	        dataset_name_override: Optional dataset name override for display.
    68	        config: ChartConfig for customization across all charts.
    69	        output_dir: Directory used for chart persistence when saving is enabled.
    70	        save: Whether chart persistence is enabled.
    71	        cache: PredictionCache for caching aggregated results.
    72	        default_aggregate: Default aggregation mode for all visualization methods.
    73	
    74	    Example:
    75	        >>> from nirs4all.data.predictions import Predictions
    76	        >>> predictions = Predictions.load('predictions.json')
    77	        >>> analyzer = PredictionAnalyzer(predictions)
    78	        >>>
    79	        >>> # Plot top 5 models - first call computes aggregation
    80	        >>> fig = analyzer.plot_top_k(k=5, aggregate='ID')
    81	        >>>
    82	        >>> # Plot heatmap - uses cached aggregation (fast!)
    83	        >>> fig = analyzer.plot_heatmap('model_name', 'preprocessings', aggregate='ID')
    84	        >>>
    85	        >>> # Check cache stats
    86	        >>> print(analyzer.get_cache_stats())
    87	        >>>
    88	        >>> # Reuse one aggregation mode across plots when desired
    89	        >>> runner = PipelineRunner()
    90	        >>> predictions, _ = runner.run(pipeline, DatasetConfigs({"train_x": path, "aggregate": "sample_id"}))
    91	        >>> analyzer = PredictionAnalyzer(predictions, default_aggregate=True)
    92	        >>> fig = analyzer.plot_top_k(k=5)  # Aggregated by the repetition column
    93	        >>> saver = PredictionAnalyzer(predictions, output_dir="workspace/figures")
    94	        >>> saver.plot_top_k(k=5)
    95	    """
    96	
    97	    def __init__(
    98	        self,
    99	        predictions_obj: Predictions,
   100	        dataset_name_override: str | None = None,
   101	        config: ChartConfig | None = None,
   102	        output_dir: str | None = None,
   103	        save: bool = False,
   104	        cache_size: int = 50,
   105	        default_aggregate: bool | str | None = None,
   106	        default_aggregate_method: str | None = None,
   107	        default_aggregate_exclude_outliers: bool = False
   108	    ):
   109	        """Initialize analyzer with predictions object.
   110	
   111	        Args:
   112	            predictions_obj: The predictions object containing prediction data.
   113	            dataset_name_override: Optional dataset name override for display.
   114	            config: Optional ChartConfig for customization across all charts.
   115	            output_dir: Directory to save generated charts. When omitted, charts
   116	                stay in-memory unless ``save=True`` is requested.
   117	            save: Whether to persist generated charts. If True and output_dir is
   118	                omitted, uses NIRS4ALL_WORKSPACE/figures or "workspace/figures".
   119	            cache_size: Maximum number of cached query results. Defaults to 50.
   120	            default_aggregate: Default aggregation mode for all visualization methods.
   121	                If set, all plots will use this aggregation unless overridden.
   122	                Can be ``True`` (use the dataset repetition column), ``"y"``
   123	                (aggregate by target values), or a metadata column name.
   124	                When omitted, plots default to no aggregation.
   125	            default_aggregate_method: Default aggregation method for all visualization methods.
   126	                - None (default): Use 'mean' for regression, 'vote' for classification
   127	                - 'mean': Average predictions within each group
   128	                - 'median': Median prediction within each group
   129	                - 'vote': Majority voting (for classification)
   130	            default_aggregate_exclude_outliers: If True, exclude outliers using T² statistic
   131	                before aggregation (default: False).
   132	
   133	        Example:
   134	            >>> analyzer = PredictionAnalyzer(predictions, default_aggregate="sample_id")
   135	            >>> fig = analyzer.plot_top_k(k=5)  # Aggregated by sample_id
   136	            >>> fig = analyzer.plot_top_k(k=5, aggregate=False)  # Explicit override to no aggregation
   137	            >>> saver = PredictionAnalyzer(predictions, save=True)
   138	            >>> saver.plot_top_k(k=5)
   139	        """
   140	        self.predictions = predictions_obj
   141	        self.dataset_name_override = dataset_name_override
   142	        self.config = config or ChartConfig()
   143	        self.save = save or output_dir is not None
   144	        self.output_dir = output_dir if output_dir is not None else (_get_default_figures_dir() if self.save else None)
   145	        self._cache = PredictionCache(max_entries=cache_size)
   146	        self.default_aggregate = default_aggregate
   147	        self.default_aggregate_method = default_aggregate_method
   148	        self.default_aggregate_exclude_outliers = default_aggregate_exclude_outliers
   149	
   150	    def clear_cache(self) -> None:
   151	        """Clear all caches.
   152	
   153	        Call this if the underlying predictions data has been modified
   154	        to ensure fresh results are computed.
   155	        """
   156	        self._cache.clear()
   157	        clear_caches = getattr(self.predictions, "clear_caches", None)
   158	        if callable(clear_caches):
   159	            clear_caches()
   160	
   161	    def _get_predictions_context_value(self, attribute: str) -> Any:
   162	        """Safely resolve a predictions context attribute or property."""
   163	        value = getattr(self.predictions, attribute, None)
   164	        if callable(value):
   165	            with contextlib.suppress(Exception):
   166	                value = value()
   167	        return value
   168	
   169	    def _resolve_aggregate(self, aggregate: bool | str | None) -> str | None:
   170	        """Resolve effective aggregate value, considering default.
   171	
   172	        Args:
   173	            aggregate: Explicit aggregate value passed to method.
   174	                - ``None``: Use ``default_aggregate`` if one was configured.
   175	                - ``False`` / ``""``: Disable aggregation.
   176	                - ``True``: Use the dataset repetition column when available.
   177	                - ``"y"`` / explicit column name: Aggregate by that key.
   178	
   179	        Returns:
   180	            Effective aggregate column name or None.
   181	        """
   182	        effective = self.default_aggregate if aggregate is None else aggregate
   183	
   184	        if effective in (None, False, ""):
   185	            return None
   186	
   187	        if effective is True:
   188	            repetition_column = self._get_predictions_context_value("repetition_column")
   189	            if isinstance(repetition_column, str) and repetition_column:
   190	                return repetition_column
   191	            return None
   192	
   193	        return str(effective)
   194	
   195	    def _resolve_aggregate_method(self, method: str | None) -> str | None:
   196	        """Resolve effective aggregate method, considering default.
   197	
   198	        Args:
   199	            method: Explicit method value passed to method.
   200	                - None: Use default_aggregate_method (if set).
   201	                - Explicit value: Use that value (overrides default).
   202	
   203	        Returns:
   204	            Effective aggregate method or None.
   205	        """
   206	        if method is not None:
   207	            return method
   208	        return self.default_aggregate_method
   209	
   210	    def _resolve_aggregate_exclude_outliers(self, exclude: bool | None) -> bool:
   211	        """Resolve effective aggregate exclude_outliers, considering default.
   212	
   213	        Args:
   214	            exclude: Explicit exclude_outliers value passed to method.
   215	                - None: Use default_aggregate_exclude_outliers.
   216	                - Explicit value: Use that value (overrides default).
   217	
   218	        Returns:
   219	            Effective exclude_outliers setting.
   220	        """
   221	        if exclude is not None:
   222	            return exclude
   223	        return self.default_aggregate_exclude_outliers
   224	
   225	    def get_cache_stats(self) -> dict[str, Any]:
   226	        """Get cache performance statistics.
   227	
   228	        Returns:
   229	            Dictionary with stats for analyzer cache and any optional
   230	            prediction-level cache implementation:
   231	            - analyzer_cache: Query result cache stats
   232	            - ranker_cache: Aggregation and score cache stats (if exposed)
   233	        """
   234	        get_cache_stats = getattr(self.predictions, "get_cache_stats", None)
   235	        ranker_cache = get_cache_stats() if callable(get_cache_stats) else {}
   236	        return {
   237	            'analyzer_cache': self._cache.get_stats(),
   238	            'ranker_cache': ranker_cache,
   239	        }
   240	
   241	    def get_cached_predictions(
   242	        self,
   243	        n: int,
   244	        rank_metric: str,
   245	        rank_partition: str = 'val',

   248	        display_metrics: list[str] | None = None,

   255	    ):
   256	        """Get predictions with caching support.

     1	"""
     2	Module-level predict() function for nirs4all.
     3	
     4	This module provides a simple interface for making predictions with trained
     5	nirs4all models. It wraps PipelineRunner.predict() with ergonomic defaults.
     6	
     7	Two prediction paths are supported:
     8	
     9	1. **Store-based** (preferred): ``nirs4all.predict(chain_id="abc", data=X)``
    10	   replays a stored chain directly from the workspace store.
    11	
    12	2. **Model-based** (legacy): ``nirs4all.predict(model="model.n4a", data=X)``
    13	   resolves via PredictionResolver / BundleLoader.
    14	
    15	Example:
    16	    >>> import nirs4all
    17	    >>> result = nirs4all.predict(
    18	    ...     model="exports/best_model.n4a",
    19	    ...     data=X_new,
    20	    ...     verbose=1
    21	    ... )
    22	    >>> print(f"Predictions shape: {result.shape}")
    23	"""
    24	
    25	from __future__ import annotations
    26	
    27	from pathlib import Path
    28	from typing import Any, TypeAlias
    29	
    30	import numpy as np
    31	
    32	from nirs4all.data import DatasetConfigs
    33	from nirs4all.data.dataset import SpectroDataset
    34	from nirs4all.pipeline import PipelineRunner
    35	
    36	from .result import PredictResult
    37	from .session import Session
    38	
    39	# Type aliases for clarity
    40	ModelSpec: TypeAlias = (
    41	    dict[str, Any]               # Prediction dict from previous run
    42	    | str                          # Path to bundle (.n4a) or config
    43	    | Path                          # Path to bundle or config
    44	)
    45	
    46	DataSpec: TypeAlias = (
    47	    str                          # Path to data folder
    48	    | Path                         # Path to data folder
    49	    | np.ndarray                   # X array
    50	    | tuple[np.ndarray, ...]       # (X,) or (X, y)
    51	    | dict[str, Any]               # Dict with X key
    52	    | SpectroDataset               # Direct SpectroDataset instance
    53	    | DatasetConfigs                # Backward compat
    54	)
    55	
    56	def predict(
    57	    model: ModelSpec | None = None,
    58	    data: DataSpec | None = None,
    59	    *,
    60	    chain_id: str | None = None,
    61	    workspace_path: str | Path | None = None,
    62	    name: str = "prediction_dataset",
    63	    all_predictions: bool = False,
    64	    session: Session | None = None,
    65	    verbose: int = 0,
    66	    **runner_kwargs: Any,
    67	) -> PredictResult:
    68	    """Make predictions with a trained model on new data.
    69	
    70	    This function provides a simple interface for running inference with
    71	    trained nirs4all pipelines.
    72	
    73	    Two prediction paths are supported:
    74	
    75	    **Store-based** (preferred) -- pass ``chain_id`` together with a
    76	    raw numpy array for ``data``:
    77	
    78	    >>> result = nirs4all.predict(chain_id="abc123", data=X_new)
    79	
    80	    **Model-based** (legacy) -- pass ``model`` together with ``data``:
    81	
    82	    >>> result = nirs4all.predict(model="exports/model.n4a", data=X_new)
    83	
    84	    Args:
    85	        model: Trained model specification. Can be:
    86	            - Prediction dict from ``result.best`` or ``result.top()``
    87	            - Path to exported bundle: ``"exports/model.n4a"``
    88	            - Path to pipeline config directory
    89	            Mutually exclusive with ``chain_id``.
    90	
    91	        data: Data to predict on. Can be:
    92	            - Path to data folder: ``"new_data/"``
    93	            - Numpy array: ``X_new`` (n_samples, n_features)
    94	            - Tuple: ``(X,)`` or ``(X, y)`` for evaluation
    95	            - Dict: ``{"X": X, "metadata": meta}``
    96	            - SpectroDataset instance
    97	
    98	        chain_id: Chain identifier in the workspace store.
    99	            When provided, uses the fast store-based replay path.
   100	            Mutually exclusive with ``model``.
   101	
   102	        workspace_path: Workspace root directory.  Required when using
   103	            ``chain_id`` outside a session.  Ignored when a ``session``
   104	            is provided (the session's workspace is used instead).
   105	
   106	        name: Name for the prediction dataset (for logging).
   107	            Default: "prediction_dataset"
   108	
   109	        all_predictions: If True, return predictions from all folds.
   110	            If False (default), return single aggregated prediction.
   111	
   112	        session: Optional Session for resource reuse.
   113	            If provided, uses the session's runner.
   114	
   115	        verbose: Verbosity level (0=quiet, 1=info, 2=debug).
   116	            Default: 0
   117	
   118	        **runner_kwargs: Additional PipelineRunner parameters.
   119	            Common options: plots_visible
   120

   214	class RunResult:
   215	    """Result from nirs4all.run().
   216	
   217	    Provides convenient access to predictions, best model, and artifacts.
   218	    Wraps the raw (predictions, per_dataset) tuple returned by PipelineRunner.run().
   219	
   220	    Attributes:
   221	        predictions: Predictions object containing all pipeline results.
   222	        per_dataset: Dictionary with per-dataset execution details.
   223	
   224	    Properties:
   225	        best: Best prediction entry by default ranking.
   226	        best_score: Best model's primary test score (CV selection metric).
   227	        best_rmse: Best model's RMSE (regression).
   228	        best_r2: Best model's R² (regression).
   229	        best_accuracy: Best model's accuracy (classification).
   230	        final: Refit model prediction entry (``fold_id="final"``), or ``None``.
   231	        final_score: Refit model test score, or ``None`` if no refit.
   232	        cv_best: Best CV prediction entry.
   233	        cv_best_score: Best CV validation score.
   234	        models: Per-model refit results (for Phase 2, one entry).
   235	        artifacts_path: Path to run artifacts directory.
   236	        num_predictions: Total number of predictions stored.
   237	
   238	    Key Operations:
   239	        top(n): Get top N predictions by ranking.
   240	        export(path): Export best model to .n4a bundle.
   241	        filter(**kwargs): Filter predictions by criteria.
   242	        get_datasets(): Get list of unique dataset names.
   243	        get_models(): Get list of unique model names.
   244	
   245	    Example:
   246	        >>> result = nirs4all.run(pipeline, dataset)
   247	        >>> print(f"Best RMSE: {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
   248	        >>> print(f"Best R²: {result.best_r2:.4f}")
   249	        >>> result.export("exports/best_model.n4a")
   250	    """
   251	
   252	    predictions: Predictions
   253	    per_dataset: dict[str, Any]
   254	    _runner: PipelineRunner | None = field(default=None, repr=False)
   255	    _owns_runner: bool = field(default=True, repr=False)
   256	    _workspace_path: Path | None = field(default=None, repr=False)
   257	
   258	    # Lazy refit dependencies (set by the orchestrator when per-model
   259	    # selections are available so that ``models`` returns lazy results)
   260	    _per_model_selections: dict[str, PerModelSelection] | None = field(default=None, repr=False)
   261	    _refit_config: RefitConfig | None = field(default=None, repr=False)
   262	    _refit_dataset: Any = field(default=None, repr=False)
   263	    _refit_context: Any = field(default=None, repr=False)
   264	    _refit_runtime_context: Any = field(default=None, repr=False)
   265	    _refit_artifact_registry: Any = field(default=None, repr=False)
   266	    _refit_executor: Any = field(default=None, repr=False)
   267	
   268	    # --- Lifecycle ---
   269	
   270	    def detach(self) -> None:
   271	        """Detach from the runner by closing its store and dropping the reference.
   272	
   273	        After detaching, the RunResult operates in detached mode: export
   274	        operations re-open the store on demand.  This releases the DB
   275	        connection so other processes can access the workspace.
   276	
   277	        Called automatically by :func:`nirs4all.run` for non-session runs.
   278	        """
   279	        if self._runner is not None and self._owns_runner:
   280	            if self._workspace_path is None:
   281	                self._workspace_path = getattr(self._runner, 'workspace_path', None)
   282	            self._runner.close()
   283	            self._runner = None
   284	
   285	    def close(self) -> None:
   286	        """Close the underlying WorkspaceStore to release DB resources.
   287	
   288	        Safe to call multiple times.  For detached results this is a no-op.
   289	        Session-owned runners are closed by the session.
   290	        """
   291	        if self._runner is not None and self._owns_runner:
   292	            self._runner.close()
   293	
   294	    def __enter__(self) -> RunResult:
   295	        return self
   296	
   297	    def __exit__(self, *exc: object) -> None:
   298	        self.close()
   299	
   300	    def __del__(self) -> None:
   301	        """Safety net: close store if caller forgot."""
   302	        with contextlib.suppress(Exception):
   303	            self.close()
   304	
   305	    # --- Primary accessors ---
   306	
   307	    @property
   308	    def best(self) -> dict[str, Any]:
   309	        """Get the best prediction entry, preferring refit (final) models.
   310	
   311	        When refit entries exist, returns the best final entry.
   312	        Otherwise falls back to the best CV entry.
   313	
   314	        Returns:
   315	            Dictionary containing best model's metrics, name, and configuration.
   316	            Empty dict if no predictions available.
   317	        """
   318	        final = self.best_final
   319	        if final:
   320	            return final
   321	        return self.cv_best
   322	
   323	    @property
   324	    def best_score(self) -> float:
   325	        """Get best model's primary test score.
   326	
   327	        Returns:
   328	            The test_score value from best prediction, or NaN if unavailable.
   329	        """
   330	        score = self.best.get('test_score')
   331	        return float(score) if score is not None else float('nan')
   332	
   333	    @property
   334	    def best_rmse(self) -> float:
   335	        """Get best model's RMSE score.
   336	
   337	        Looks for 'rmse' as a flat key (from display_metrics), then in scores dict,
   338	        then falls back to test_score if metric is rmse-like.
   339	
   340	        Returns:
   341	            RMSE value or NaN if unavailable.
   342	        """
   343	        entry = self.predictions.get_best(metric="rmse", task_type="regression", score_scope="all")
   344	        best = entry if entry else self.best
   345	        if not best:
   346	            return float('nan')
   347	
   348	        # Try flat 'rmse' key first (from display_metrics)
   349	        if 'rmse' in best and best['rmse'] is not None:
   350	            return float(best['rmse'])
   351	
   352	        # Try nested scores dict (legacy format)
   353	        scores = best.get('scores', {})
   354	        if isinstance(scores, dict):
   355	            test_scores = scores.get('test', {})
   356	            if 'rmse' in test_scores and test_scores['rmse'] is not None:
   357	                return float(test_scores['rmse'])
   358	
   359	        # Fall back to test_score if metric is rmse-like
   360	        metric = best.get('metric', '')

     3	# Builds docs with Sphinx and checks for broken links
     4	
     5	name: Documentation
     6	
     7	on:
     8	  push:
     9	    branches: [main, master]
    10	    paths:
    11	      - 'docs/**'
    12	      - 'nirs4all/**'
    13	      - '.github/workflows/docs.yml'
    14	      - '.readthedocs.yaml'
    15	  pull_request:
    16	    branches: [main, master]
    17	    paths:
    18	      - 'docs/**'
    19	      - 'nirs4all/**'
    20	      - '.github/workflows/docs.yml'
    21	  workflow_dispatch:  # Allow manual trigger
    22	
    23	jobs:
    24	  build-docs:
    25	    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    26	    steps:
    27	      - name: Free disk space
    28	        run: |
    29	          sudo rm -rf /usr/share/dotnet /usr/local/lib/android /opt/ghc /opt/hostedtoolcache/CodeQL
    30	          sudo docker image prune --all --force
    31	
    32	      - name: Checkout repository
    33	        uses: actions/checkout@v6
    34	
    35	      - name: Set up Python
    36	        uses: actions/setup-python@v6
    37	        with:
    38	          python-version: '3.11'
    39	          cache: 'pip'
    40	
    41	      - name: Install documentation dependencies
    42	        run: |
    43	          python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
    44	          python -m pip install -r docs/readthedocs.requirements.txt
    45	
    46	      - name: Install nirs4all package
    47	        run: python -m pip install -e .
    48	
    49	      - name: Build documentation
    50	        run: |
    51	          cd docs
    52	          sphinx-build -b html source _build/html -W --keep-going 2>&1 | tee build.log
    53	
    54	      - name: Check for build warnings
    55	        run: |
    56	          if grep -q "WARNING" docs/build.log; then
    57	            echo "::warning::Documentation build produced warnings"
    58	            grep "WARNING" docs/build.log || true
    59	          fi
    60	
    61	      - name: Upload documentation artifacts
    62	        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v7
    63	        with:
    64	          name: documentation-html
    65	          path: docs/_build/html/
    66	          retention-days: 7
    67	
    68	  linkcheck:
    69	    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    70	    needs: build-docs
    71	    steps:
    72	      - name: Free disk space
    73	        run: |
    74	          sudo rm -rf /usr/share/dotnet /usr/local/lib/android /opt/ghc /opt/hostedtoolcache/CodeQL
    75	          sudo docker image prune --all --force
    76	
    77	      - name: Checkout repository
    78	        uses: actions/checkout@v6
    79	
    80	      - name: Set up Python
    81	        uses: actions/setup-python@v6
    82	        with:
    83	          python-version: '3.11'
    84	          cache: 'pip'
    85	
    86	      - name: Install dependencies
    87	        run: |
    88	          python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
    89	          python -m pip install -r docs/readthedocs.requirements.txt
    90	          python -m pip install -e .
    91	
    92	      - name: Check external links
    93	        run: |
    94	          cd docs
    95	          sphinx-build -b linkcheck source _build/linkcheck -W --keep-going 2>&1 | tee linkcheck.log
    96	
    97	      - name: Report broken links
    98	        run: |
    99	          if [ -f docs/_build/linkcheck/output.txt ]; then
   100	            echo "=== Link Check Results ==="
   101	            cat docs/_build/linkcheck/output.txt
   102	
   103	            # Count broken links
   104	            broken=$(grep -c "\[broken\]" docs/_build/linkcheck/output.txt || echo "0")
   105	            if [ "$broken" -gt "0" ]; then
   106	              echo "::warning::Found $broken broken link(s)"
   107	            fi
   108	          fi
   109	
   110	      - name: Upload linkcheck report
   111	        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v7
   112	        with:
   113	          name: linkcheck-report
   114	          path: docs/_build/linkcheck/
   115	          retention-days: 7

   226	        """Deserialize an operator value if needed.
   227	
   228	        Handles:
   229	        - None: returns None
   230	        - Instances: returns as-is
   231	        - Class types: returns as-is (controller will instantiate)
   232	        - Dict with 'class'/'function': deserializes component
   233	        - String: deserializes as module path

   237	            return None

   252	| Keyword | Description |
   253	|---------|-------------|
   254	| `augment_chart` / `augmentation_chart` | Overlay of original vs augmented |
   255	| `augment_details_chart` / `augmentation_details_chart` | Grid showing each augmentation type |
   256	
   257	### Usage
   258	
   259	```python
   260	from nirs4all.operators.augmentation import GaussianNoise, SpectrumShift
   261	
   262	pipeline = [
   263	    {"sample_augmentation": [GaussianNoise(sigma=0.01), SpectrumShift(max_shift=5)]},
   264	    "augment_chart",             # Overlay view
   265	    "augment_details_chart",     # Detailed grid view
   266	    ShuffleSplit(n_splits=3),
   267	    PLSRegression(n_components=10),
   268	]
   269	```
   270	
   271	### Overlay Chart (`augment_chart`)
   272	
   273	Shows original spectra with augmented versions overlaid:
   274	- Original samples in solid lines
   275	- Augmented samples in dashed lines with different colors
   276	
   277	```{figure} ../../assets/augment_chart.png
   278	:align: center
   279	:width: 90%
   280	:alt: Augmentation Chart
   281	
   282	Overlay of original and augmented spectra.
   283	```
   284	
   285	### Details Chart (`augment_details_chart`)
   286	
   287	Shows a grid with one subplot per augmentation type:
   288	- First panel: Raw (original) spectra
   289	- Subsequent panels: Each augmentation technique separately
   290	
   291	```{figure} ../../assets/augment_details_chart.png
   292	:align: center
   293	:width: 90%
   294	:alt: Augmentation Details Chart
   295	
   296	Grid showing each augmentation type separately.
   297	```
   298	
   299	### Multiple Augmentation Methods
   300	
   301	When using multiple augmentation transformers, the details chart shows each method:
   302	
   303	```python
   304	from nirs4all.operators.augmentation import GaussianAdditiveNoise, WavelengthShift
   305

    77

     1	"""
     2	DatasetConfigs - Configuration and caching for dataset loading.
     3	
     4	This module provides DatasetConfigs class that handles dataset configuration,
     5	name resolution, loader calls, and caching to avoid reloading the same dataset.
     6	"""
     7	
     8	import copy
     9	import hashlib
    10	import json
    11	from typing import Any, Optional, Union
    12	
    13	from nirs4all.core.logging import get_logger
    14	from nirs4all.data.dataset import SpectroDataset
    15	
    16	logger = get_logger(__name__)
    17	from nirs4all.data.config_parser import parse_config
    18	from nirs4all.data.loaders.loader import handle_data
    19	from nirs4all.data.signal_type import SignalType, SignalTypeInput, normalize_signal_type
    20	
    21	
    22	class DatasetConfigs:
    23	
    24	    def __init__(
    25	        self,
    26	        configurations: dict[str, Any] | list[dict[str, Any]] | str | list[str],
    27	        task_type: str | list[str] = "auto",
    28	        signal_type: SignalTypeInput | list[SignalTypeInput] | None = None,
    29	        repetition: str | list[str | None] | None = None,
    30	        aggregate: str | bool | list[str | bool | None] | None = None,
    31	        aggregate_method: str | list[str] | None = None,
    32	        aggregate_exclude_outliers: bool | list[bool] | None = None
    33	    ):
    34	        '''Initialize dataset configurations.
    35	
    36	        Args:
    37	            configurations: Dataset configuration(s) as path(s), dict(s), or list of either.
    38	                Configuration dicts can include:
    39	                - 'task_type': "regression", "binary_classification", "multiclass_classification", "auto"
    40	                - 'aggregate': Sample aggregation column name, True for y-based, or None
    41	                - 'train_x_params' or 'global_params' with:
    42	                    - header_unit: "cm-1", "nm", "none", "text", "index"
    43	                    - signal_type: "absorbance", "reflectance", "reflectance%", "transmittance", etc.
    44	                    - delimiter, decimal_separator, has_header, na_policy, etc.
    45	
    46	            task_type: Force task type. Can be:
    47	                - A single string applied to all datasets
    48	                - A list of strings (one per dataset)
    49	                Valid values per dataset:
    50	                - 'auto': Use config value or automatic detection (default)
    51	                - 'regression': Force regression task
    52	                - 'binary_classification': Force binary classification task
    53	                - 'multiclass_classification': Force multiclass classification task
    54	                Note: Constructor parameter overrides config dict value (except 'auto').
    55	
    56	            signal_type: Override signal type for spectral data (applied after config loading).
    57	                - A single value applied to all datasets/sources
    58	                - A list of values (one per dataset)
    59	                - None: Use config value or auto-detect (default)
    60	                This parameter overrides any signal_type specified in the config.
    61	                Valid values: 'absorbance', 'reflectance', 'reflectance%',
    62	                'transmittance', 'transmittance%', 'auto', etc.
    63	
    64	            repetition: Column name identifying sample repetitions (multiple spectral
    65	                measurements of the same physical sample).
    66	                - None (default): No repetition grouping
    67	                - str: Metadata column name (e.g., 'Sample_ID', 'ID')
    68	                - list: Per-dataset settings (must match number of datasets)
    69	                When set, splits will automatically group by this column to prevent
    70	                data leakage, and prediction aggregation is automatically enabled
    71	                using the same column. This is the preferred way to handle repeated
    72	                measurements.
    73	
    74	            aggregate: Aggregation column for prediction reporting. Normally set
    75	                automatically from ``repetition``. Use this parameter only when
    76	                the aggregation column differs from the repetition column.
    77	                - None (default): Inherit from ``repetition`` if set, otherwise no aggregation
    78	                - True: Aggregate by target values (y_true)
    79	                - str: Aggregate by specified metadata column
    80	                - list: Per-dataset settings (must match number of datasets)
    81	
    82	            aggregate_method: Aggregation method for combining predictions.
    83	                - None (default): Use 'mean' for regression, 'vote' for classification
    84	                - 'mean': Average predictions within each group
    85	                - 'median': Median prediction within each group
    86	                - 'vote': Majority voting (for classification)
    87	                - list: Per-dataset methods (must match number of datasets)
    88	
    89	            aggregate_exclude_outliers: Whether to exclude outliers before aggregation.
    90	                Uses Hotelling's T² statistic to identify and exclude outlier
    91	                measurements within each sample group before averaging.
    92	                - None/False (default): No outlier exclusion
    93	                - True: Exclude outliers using T² with 0.95 confidence
    94	                - list: Per-dataset settings (must match number of datasets)
    95	
    96	        Example:
    97	            # Via config dict (preferred for per-source control):
    98	            config = {
    99	                "train_x": "/path/to/data.csv",
   100	                "task_type": "regression",
   101	                "repetition": "sample_id",
   102	                "train_x_params": {
   103	                    "header_unit": "nm",
   104	                    "signal_type": "reflectance",
   105	                    "delimiter": ";"
   106	                }
   107	            }
   108	            configs = DatasetConfigs(config)
   109	
   110	            # Or via constructor parameter (overrides config):
   111	            configs = DatasetConfigs("/path/to/folder", task_type="regression")
   112	            configs = DatasetConfigs("/path/to/folder", signal_type="absorbance")
   113	            configs = DatasetConfigs("/path/to/folder", repetition="sample_id")
   114	        '''
   115	        user_configs = configurations if isinstance(configurations, list) else [configurations]
   116	        self.configs = []
   117	        self._config_task_types: list[str | None] = []  # task_type from config dicts
   118	        self._config_aggregates: list[str | bool | None] = []  # aggregate from config dicts
   119	        self._config_aggregate_methods: list[str | None] = []  # aggregate_method from config dicts
   120	        self._config_aggregate_exclude_outliers: list[bool | None] = []  # aggregate_exclude_outliers from config dicts

     1	"""
     2	Dataset configuration parser.
     3	
     4	This module provides functions for parsing dataset configurations from various formats.
     5	It serves as the main entry point for configuration parsing, delegating to specialized
     6	parsers in the nirs4all.data.parsers module.
     7	
     8	The parser supports:
     9	- Folder paths with auto-scanning for data files
    10	- JSON/YAML configuration files
    11	- Dictionary configurations (train_x/test_x format)
    12	- In-memory numpy arrays
    13	
    14	For schema-based validation, see nirs4all.data.schema.
    15	For specialized parsers, see nirs4all.data.parsers.
    16	"""
    17	
    18	import json
    19	from pathlib import Path
    20	from typing import Any, Optional
    21	
    22	import numpy as np
    23	import yaml
    24	
    25	from nirs4all.core.logging import get_logger
    26	from nirs4all.data.parsers.normalizer import ConfigNormalizer
    27	
    28	logger = get_logger(__name__)
    29	
    30	# Create shared normalizer instance
    31	_normalizer = ConfigNormalizer()
    32	
    33	def _load_config_from_file(file_path: str) -> tuple[dict[str, Any] | None, str]:
    34	    """Load dataset config from JSON/YAML file.
    35	
    36	    Args:
    37	        file_path: Path to a JSON or YAML configuration file.
    38	
    39	    Returns:
    40	        Tuple of (config_dict, dataset_name).
    41	
    42	    Raises:
    43	        FileNotFoundError: If the config file does not exist.
    44	        ValueError: If the file contains invalid JSON/YAML or is empty.
    45	    """
    46	    return _normalizer._load_config_file(file_path)
    47	
    48	def _s_(path):
    49	    """Convert path(s) to POSIX format. Handles both single paths and lists of paths."""
    50	    if path is None:
    51	        return None
    52	    if isinstance(path, list):
    53	        return [Path(p).as_posix() for p in path]
    54	    return Path(path).as_posix()
    55	
    56	def browse_folder(folder_path, global_params=None):
    57	    """Scan a folder for data files matching standard naming conventions.
    58	
    59	    This function delegates to FolderParser for the actual scanning.
    60	
    61	    Args:
    62	        folder_path: Path to folder to scan.
    63	        global_params: Optional global loading parameters.
    64	
    65	    Returns:
    66	        Configuration dictionary with detected file paths.
    67	    """
    68	    from nirs4all.data.parsers.folder_parser import FolderParser
    69	
    70	    parser = FolderParser()
    71	
    72	    # Create input for parser
    73	    input_data = {"folder": folder_path, "global_params": global_params} if global_params is not None else folder_path
    74	
    75	    result = parser.parse(input_data)
    76	
    77	    if result.success:
    78	        return result.config
    79	
    80	    # Return empty config on failure (backward compatible behavior)
    81	    logger.error(f"Failed to browse folder {folder_path}: {result.errors}")
    82	    return {
    83	        "train_x": None, "train_x_filter": None, "train_x_params": None,
    84	        "train_y": None, "train_y_filter": None, "train_y_params": None,
    85	        "train_group": None, "train_group_filter": None, "train_group_params": None,
    86	        "train_params": None,
    87	        "test_x": None, "test_x_filter": None, "test_x_params": None,
    88	        "test_y": None, "test_y_filter": None, "test_y_params": None,
    89	        "test_group": None, "test_group_filter": None, "test_group_params": None,
    90	        "test_params": None,
    91	        "global_params": global_params
    92	    }
    93	
    94	def folder_to_name(folder_path):
    95	    """Extract a dataset name from a folder path.
    96	
    97	    Args:
    98	        folder_path: Path to folder.
    99	
   100	    Returns:
   101	        Cleaned dataset name.
   102	    """
   103	    path = Path(folder_path)
   104	    for part in reversed(path.parts):
   105	        clean_part = ''.join(c if c.isalnum() else '_' for c in part)
   106	        if clean_part:
   107	            return clean_part.lower()
   108	    return "Unknown_dataset"
   109	
   110	def parse_config(data_config):
   111	    """Parse a dataset configuration.
   112	
   113	    Handles multiple input formats:
   114	    - String path to a folder: auto-browse for data files
   115	    - String path to JSON/YAML file (.json, .yaml, .yml): load config from file
   116	    - Dict with 'folder' key: browse folder with optional params
   117	    - Dict with data keys (train_x, test_x, etc.): use directly
   118	
   119	    Args:
   120	        data_config: Dataset configuration in any supported format.
   121	
   122	    Returns:
   123	        Tuple of (parsed_config_dict, dataset_name).
   124	        Returns (None, 'Unknown_dataset') if parsing fails.
   125	    """
   126	    # Use the new normalizer for unified handling
   127	    return _normalizer.normalize(data_config)
   128

  1256	
  1257	**Key difference from sequential steps**:
  1258	- A **single pipeline** `[step1, step2, step3]` executes steps sequentially
  1259	- A **list of pipelines** `[[step1, step2], [step3, step4]]` executes each pipeline **independently**
  1260	
  1261	### Cartesian Product: Pipelines × Datasets
  1262	
  1263	When you also provide multiple datasets, `nirs4all.run()` executes the **cartesian product**:
  1264	
  1265	```python
  1266	result = nirs4all.run(
  1267	    pipeline=[pipeline_pls, pipeline_rf],   # 2 pipelines
  1268	    dataset=["data/wheat", "data/corn"],    # 2 datasets
  1269	    verbose=1
  1270	)

  1237	    def get_feature_importance(
  1238	        self,
  1239	        top_n: int | None = None,
  1240	        normalize: bool = False
  1241	    ) -> dict[str, float]:
  1242	        """Get feature importance ranking.
  1243	
  1244	        Args:
  1245	            top_n: If provided, return only top N features.
  1246	            normalize: If True, normalize values to sum to 1.
  1247	
  1248	        Returns:
  1249	            Dictionary mapping feature names to importance values.
  1250	        """

  1259	            sorted_indices = sorted_indices[:top_n]

  1261	        result = {}
  1262	        for idx in sorted_indices:
  1263	            name = self.feature_names[idx] if self.feature_names else str(idx)
  1264	            result[name] = float(importance[idx])

   130	    Raises:
   131	        ValueError: If neither ``model`` nor ``chain_id`` is provided,
   132	            or if both are provided.
   133	        FileNotFoundError: If model bundle or data path doesn't exist.
   134	
   135	    Examples:
   136	        Predict from a stored chain (preferred):
   137	
   138	        >>> import nirs4all
   139	        >>> result = nirs4all.predict(chain_id="abc123", data=X_new)
   140	
   141	        Predict from an exported bundle:
   142

   145	        ...     data=X_new
   146	        ... )

   148	        Predict using a result from a previous run:
   149	
   150	        >>> train_result = nirs4all.run(pipeline, train_data)
   151	        >>> pred_result = nirs4all.predict(
   152	        ...     model=train_result.best,
   153	        ...     data=X_test
   154	        ... )
   155

   157	        - :func:`nirs4all.run`: Train a pipeline
   158	        - :func:`nirs4all.explain`: Generate SHAP explanations
   159	        - :class:`nirs4all.api.result.PredictResult`: Result class
   160	    """
   161	    # ---- Validate mutually exclusive arguments ----
   162	    if model is not None and chain_id is not None:
   163	        raise ValueError("Provide either 'model' or 'chain_id', not both.")

   178	        )

**Confirmed Spot-Checks**
- CONFIRMED #3: `result.predict()` is documented at `docs/source/getting_started/index.md:192`, but `RunResult` starts at `nirs4all/api/result.py:214` and its public methods are `top/filter/get_datasets/get_models/export/...` at `api/result.py:605-903`; no `predict`.
- CONFIRMED #4, with nuance: `bundle=` is documented at `docs/source/user_guide/deployment/index.md:84-86`; real signature is `predict(model=None, data=None, *, chain_id=...)` at `nirs4all/api/predict.py:56-67`.
- CONFIRMED #5 scale: independent grep found 655 candidate hits across 143 files; requiring whitespace around `=` gives 605 across 128 files. The audit’s 648 is in the right ballpark.
- CONFIRMED #7: `nirs4all.load_dataset()` is shown at `docs/source/onboarding/persona_paths.md:83`; `nirs4all.__all__` at `nirs4all/__init__.py:82-113` has no `load_dataset`.
- CONFIRMED/IMPRECISE #9: docs call `plot_predictions/plot_residuals/plot_calibration` at `docs/source/user_guide/visualization/index.md:76-78`; source has `plot_top_k`, `plot_confusion_matrix`, `plot_histogram`, `plot_heatmap`, `plot_candlestick` at `nirs4all/visualization/predictions.py:533,641,755,847,994`.
- CONFIRMED/IMPRECISE #10: `GaussianNoise`, `SpectrumShift`, `OutlierExclusion` are wrong at `docs/source/user_guide/visualization/in_pipeline_charts.md:260,263,351`; real classes include `GaussianAdditiveNoise`, `WavelengthShift`, `XOutlierFilter` at `nirs4all/operators/augmentation/spectral.py:36,214` and `nirs4all/operators/filters/x_outlier.py:18`.
- CONFIRMED #12/#13/#15: `SklearnWrapper` is wrong at `docs/source/examples/user/explainability.md:189`; real export is `NIRSPipeline` at `nirs4all/sklearn/__init__.py:37-42`. `examples.synthetic` is wrong at `docs/source/user_guide/augmentation/synthetic_nirs_generator.md:405`; real class is `nirs4all/synthesis/generator.py:95`. U21/U22 refs are wrong at `docs/source/user_guide/deployment/export_bundles.md:373-374`; actual files are U01-U04.
- CONFIRMED #19: `examples.yml` has only `schedule` and `workflow_dispatch` at `.github/workflows/examples.yml:7-13`; no push/PR. Docs CI builds Sphinx only at `.github/workflows/docs.yml:49-52`, and `conf.py` has no doctest/myst-nb execution extensions.

**Corrections Needed**
- License claim is overstated. First-contact pages saying CeCILL-only are wrong, but `LICENSE:1-13` says dual licensing with default `AGPL-3.0-or-later` and optional `CeCILL-2.1`; README repeats that at `README.md:430-431`. A CI grep banning any `CeCILL` token would be wrong.
- `bundle=` will not raise `TypeError` at function binding because `predict()` has `**runner_kwargs` at `nirs4all/api/predict.py:66`; it should fail validation as neither `model` nor `chain_id` is supplied at `api/predict.py:161-165`.
- `PredictionAnalyzer` source has more than the five named methods: branch plotting methods start at `nirs4all/visualization/predictions.py:1235,1392,1549,1607,1656`. Also the quick example passes `PredictionAnalyzer(result)` at `docs/source/user_guide/visualization/index.md:73`, but constructor expects `predictions_obj: Predictions` at `nirs4all/visualization/predictions.py:97-100`.
- #11 fix is wrong. `y_column=` is unsupported, but `target_column=` is not a direct `DatasetConfigs(...)` kwarg either: constructor signature is `DatasetConfigs(configurations, task_type, signal_type, repetition, aggregate, ...)` at `nirs4all/data/config.py:24-32`. Existing docs put `target_column` inside `global_params` at `docs/source/user_guide/data/loading_data.md:47-50`.
- #22 contains a false subclaim: `ExplainResult.get_feature_importance()` exists at `nirs4all/api/result.py:1237-1241`. Keep the `predict(source, dataset)` correction, drop the fake-method claim.
- Style count should be labeled “grep candidates,” not exact violations. The grep catches compliant inline calls like `docs/source/index.md:93-99` and legitimate list-of-pipelines reuse like `docs/source/user_guide/pipelines/writing_pipelines.md:1242-1252`.
- Material miss: `nirs4all/visualization/predictions.py:76` still has a source docstring using nonexistent `Predictions.load(...)`, so generated API docs can inherit a stale API claim outside the notebook.
- Severity calibration: the two downgrades are correct. Bare classes are supported by parser docs/logic at `nirs4all/pipeline/steps/parser.py:229-246`; transfer imports are guarded by `try/except ImportError` at `examples/developer/04_transfer_learning/D01_transfer_analysis.py:130-150` and `D03_pca_geometry.py:87-96`.
